<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; font-size:smaller">
<center><big><b>Capital and most populous city of the <span class="nowrap">State of Colorado</span></b></big></center>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Denver</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span>), officially the <b>City and County of Denver</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States#State_capital" title="List of capitals in the United States">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Colorado" title="List of cities and towns in Colorado">most populous municipality</a> of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>. Denver is located in the <a href="/wiki/South_Platte_River" title="South Platte River">South Platte River Valley</a> on the western edge of the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a> just east of the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. The Denver downtown district is located immediately east of the confluence of <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Creek_(Colorado)" title="Cherry Creek (Colorado)">Cherry Creek</a> with the <a href="/wiki/South_Platte_River" title="South Platte River">South Platte River</a>, approximately 12 mi (19 km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Foothills" title="Foothills">foothills</a> of the Rocky Mountains. Denver is <a href="/wiki/List_of_city_nicknames_in_the_United_States" title="List of city nicknames in the United States">nicknamed</a> the <i>Mile-High City</i> because its official elevation is exactly one mile (5,280 ft or 1,610 m) above sea level, making it one of the highest major cities in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denfacts_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-denfacts-9">[9]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/105th_meridian_west" title="105th meridian west">105th meridian west of Greenwich</a>, the longitudinal reference for the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Time_Zone" title="Mountain Time Zone">Mountain Time Zone</a>, passes directly through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Denver,_Colorado)" title="Union Station (Denver, Colorado)">Denver Union Station</a>.</p>
<p>Denver is ranked as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpha_world_city" title="Alpha world city">Beta- world city</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network</a>. With a 2015 estimated population of 682,545, Denver ranks as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">19th-most populous U.S. city</a>, and with a 2.8% increase in 2015, the city is also the fastest growing major city in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-QF-14">[14]</a></sup> The 10-county <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Lakewood,_CO_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora-Lakewood, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Lakewood, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> had an estimated 2015 population of 2,814,330 and ranked as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">19th most populous U.S. metropolitan statistical area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-15">[15]</a></sup> The 12-city <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora,_CO_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora, CO Combined Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora, CO Combined Statistical Area</a> had an estimated 2015 population of 3,418,876, which ranks as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Combined_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Combined Statistical Areas">16th most populous U.S. metropolitan area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Denver is the most populous city of the 18-county <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>, an oblong urban region stretching across two states with an estimated 2015 population of 4,757,713.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCounties_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCounties-17">[17]</a></sup> Denver is the most populous city within a 500-mile (800 km) radius and the second-most populous city in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">Mountain West</a> after <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>. In 2016, Denver was named the best place to live in the USA by U.S. News &amp; World Report.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popular_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Popular-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Denver" title="History of Denver">History of Denver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Denver" title="Timeline of Denver">Timeline of Denver</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pd_james_w_denver.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="283" data-file-width="223" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pd_james_w_denver.jpg/170px-Pd_james_w_denver.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fd/Pd_james_w_denver.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pd_james_w_denver.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas Territorial</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/James_W._Denver" title="James W. Denver">James W. Denver</a> visited his namesake city in 1875 and in 1882.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Broncho_Buster,_Denver,_CO_IMG_5544.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Broncho_Buster%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5544.JPG/220px-Broncho_Buster%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5544.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Broncho_Buster%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5544.JPG/330px-Broncho_Buster%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5544.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Broncho_Buster%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5544.JPG/440px-Broncho_Buster%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5544.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Broncho_Buster,_Denver,_CO_IMG_5544.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Bronco Buster", a variation of <a href="/wiki/Frederic_Remington" title="Frederic Remington">Frederic Remington</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Bronco_Buster" title="Bronco Buster">Bronco Buster</a>" <a href="/wiki/Western_(genre)" title="Western (genre)">western</a> sculpture at the Denver capitol grounds, a gift from J.K. Mullen in 1920</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the summer of 1858, during the <a href="/wiki/Pike%27s_Peak_Gold_Rush" title="Pike's Peak Gold Rush">Pike's Peak Gold Rush</a>, a group of gold prospectors from <a href="/wiki/Lawrence,_Kansas" title="Lawrence, Kansas">Lawrence, Kansas</a> established <a href="/wiki/Montana_City,_Colorado" title="Montana City, Colorado">Montana City</a> as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mining_town" title="Mining town">mining town</a> on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/South_Platte_River" title="South Platte River">South Platte River</a> in what was then western <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas Territory</a>. This was the first settlement in what was later to become the city of Denver. The site faded quickly, however, and by the summer of 1859 it was abandoned in favor of <a href="/wiki/Auraria,_Denver" title="Auraria, Denver">Auraria</a> (named after the gold mining town of <a href="/wiki/Auraria,_Georgia" title="Auraria, Georgia">Auraria, Georgia</a>), and St. Charles City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 22, 1858, <a href="/wiki/William_Larimer,_Jr." title="William Larimer, Jr.">General William Larimer</a>, a land speculator from eastern <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas Territory</a>, placed <a href="/wiki/Populus_sect._Aigeiros" title="Populus sect. Aigeiros">cottonwood</a> logs to stake a claim on the bluff overlooking the confluence of the South Platte River and <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Creek_(Colorado)" title="Cherry Creek (Colorado)">Cherry Creek</a>, across the creek from the existing mining settlement of Auraria, and on the site of the existing townsite of St. Charles. Larimer named the town site Denver City to curry favor with Kansas Territorial Governor <a href="/wiki/James_W._Denver" title="James W. Denver">James W. Denver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenverHistArapaho_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-DenverHistArapaho-20">[20]</a></sup> Larimer hoped that the town's name would help make it the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of Arapaho County, but unknown to him Governor Denver had already resigned from office. The location was accessible to existing trails and was across the South Platte River from the site of seasonal encampments of the <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne" title="Cheyenne">Cheyenne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Arapaho</a>. The site of these first towns is now the site of <a href="/wiki/Confluence_Park" title="Confluence Park">Confluence Park</a> near downtown Denver. Larimer, along with associates in the St. Charles City Land Company, sold parcels in the town to merchants and miners, with the intention of creating a major city that would cater to new emigrants. Denver City was a frontier town, with an economy based on servicing local miners with gambling, saloons, livestock and goods trading. In the early years, land parcels were often traded for grubstakes or gambled away by miners in Auraria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenverHistArapaho_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-DenverHistArapaho-20">[20]</a></sup> In May 1859, Denver City residents donated 53 lots to the Leavenworth &amp; Pike's Peak Express in order to secure the region's first overland wagon route. Offering daily service for "passengers, mail, freight, and gold," the Express reached Denver on a trail that trimmed westward travel time from twelve days to six. In 1863, <a href="/wiki/Western_Union" title="Western Union">Western Union</a> furthered Denver's dominance of the region by choosing the city for its regional terminus.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Territory" title="Colorado Territory">Colorado Territory</a> was created on February 28, 1861,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateGovHistCO_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-StateGovHistCO-21">[21]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arapahoe_County,_Colorado_Territory" title="Arapahoe County, Colorado Territory">Arapahoe County</a> was formed on November 1, 1861,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateGovHistCO_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-StateGovHistCO-21">[21]</a></sup> and Denver City was incorporated on November 7, 1861.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-22">[22]</a></sup> Denver City served as the Arapahoe County Seat from 1861 until <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidation</a> in 1902.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenverHist_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-DenverHist-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1867, Denver City became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" title="Capital (political)">Territorial Capital</a>. With its new-found importance, Denver City shortened its name to Denver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenverHist_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-DenverHist-23">[23]</a></sup> On August 1, 1876, Colorado was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_date_of_statehood" title="List of U.S. states by date of statehood">admitted to the Union</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue,_Denver,_CO_IMG_5558.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5558.JPG/220px-Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5558.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5558.JPG/330px-Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5558.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5558.JPG/440px-Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue%2C_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5558.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer_Mothers_of_Colorado_statue,_Denver,_CO_IMG_5558.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Pioneer Mothers of Colorado" statue at <i><a href="/wiki/The_Denver_Post" title="The Denver Post">The Denver Post</a></i> building</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although by the close of the 1860s, Denver residents could look with pride at their success establishing a vibrant supply and service center, the decision to route the nation's first transcontinental railroad through Cheyenne, rather than Denver, threatened the prosperity of the young town. A daunting 100 miles away, citizens mobilized to build a railroad to connect Denver to the transcontinental railroad. Spearheaded by visionary leaders including Territorial Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Evans_(governor)" title="John Evans (governor)">John Evans</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Moffat" title="David Moffat">David Moffat</a>, and Walter Cheesman, fundraising began. Within three days, $300,000 had been raised, and citizens were optimistic. Fundraising stalled before enough was raised, forcing these visionary leaders to take control of the debt-ridden railroad. Despite challenges, on June 24, 1870, citizens cheered as the Denver Pacific completed the link to the transcontinental railroad, ushering in a new age of prosperity for Denver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally linked to the rest of the nation by rail, Denver prospered as a service and supply center. The young city grew during these years, attracting millionaires with their mansions, as well as the poverty and crime of a rapidly growing city. Denver citizens were proud when the rich chose Denver and were thrilled that <a href="/wiki/Horace_Tabor" title="Horace Tabor">Horace Tabor</a>, the Leadville mining millionaire, built an impressive business block at 16th and Larimer as well as the elegant Tabor Grand Opera House. Luxurious hotels, including the much-loved <a href="/wiki/Brown_Palace_Hotel_(Denver,_Colorado)" title="Brown Palace Hotel (Denver, Colorado)">Brown Palace Hotel</a>, soon followed, as well as splendid homes for millionaires like the Croke, Patterson, Campbell Mansion at 11th and Pennsylvania and the now-demolished Moffat Mansion at 8th and Grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Intent on transforming Denver into one of the world's great cities, leaders wooed industry and enticed laborers to work in these factories. Soon, in addition to the elite and a large middle class, Denver had a growing population of German, Italian, and Chinese laborers, soon followed by African-Americans and Spanish-surname workers. Unprepared for this influx, the Silver Crash of 1893 unsettled political, social, and economic balances, laying the foundation for ethnic bigotry, such as the Red Scare and the rise of the Ku Klux Klan, as well as corruption and crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1916" data-file-width="5996" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg/350px-Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg/525px-Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg/700px-Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Colorado_1898_-_LOC_-_restoration1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Panorama <a href="/wiki/Old_master_print" title="Old master print">print</a> of Denver, 1898</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1880 and 1895 the city experienced a huge rise in corruption, as crime bosses, such as <a href="/wiki/Soapy_Smith" title="Soapy Smith">Soapy Smith</a>, worked side by side with elected officials and the police to control elections, gambling, and bunco gangs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The city also experienced a <a href="/wiki/Denver_Depression_of_1893" title="Denver Depression of 1893">depression in 1893</a> after the crash of silver prices. In 1887, the precursor to the international charity <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" title="United Way of America">United Way</a> was formed in Denver by local religious leaders who raised funds and coordinated various charities to help Denver's poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> By 1890, Denver had grown to be the second-largest city west of <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In 1900, whites represented 96.8% of Denver's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1990_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-census1990-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between the 1880s and 1930s, Denver's floriculture industry developed and thrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> This period became known locally as the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Gold_Rush" title="Carnation Gold Rush">Carnation Gold Rush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1901, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_General_Assembly" title="Colorado General Assembly">Colorado General Assembly</a> voted to split Arapahoe County into three parts: a new <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidated</a> City and County of Denver, a new <a href="/wiki/Adams_County,_Colorado" title="Adams County, Colorado">Adams County</a>, and the remainder of the Arapahoe County to be renamed <a href="/wiki/South_Arapahoe_County,_Colorado" title="South Arapahoe County, Colorado">South Arapahoe County</a>. A ruling by the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Supreme_Court" title="Colorado Supreme Court">Colorado Supreme Court</a>, subsequent legislation, and a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> delayed the creation of the City and County of Denver until November 15, 1902.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Denver has hosted the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention" title="Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a> twice, during the years of <a href="/wiki/1908_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1908 Democratic National Convention">1908</a>, and again in <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008</a>, taking the opportunity to promote the city's status on the national, political, and socioeconomic stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early in the 20th century, Denver, like many other cities, was home to a pioneering <a href="/wiki/Brass_Era_car" title="Brass Era car">Brass Era car</a> company. The <a href="/wiki/Colburn_Automobile_Company" title="Colburn Automobile Company">Colburn Automobile Company</a> made cars copied from the contemporary <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1953 to 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Flats_Plant" title="Rocky Flats Plant">Rocky Flats Plant</a>, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">DOE</a> nuclear weapon facility formerly located about 15 miles from Denver, produced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fissile" title="Fissile">fissile</a> <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a> "<a href="/wiki/Pit_(nuclear_weapon)" title="Pit (nuclear weapon)">pits</a>" for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_warhead" title="Nuclear warhead">nuclear warheads</a>. A major fire at the facility in 1957, as well as leakage from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_waste" title="Nuclear waste">nuclear waste</a> stored at the site between 1958 and 1968, resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_contamination_from_the_Rocky_Flats_Plant" title="Radioactive contamination from the Rocky Flats Plant">contamination of some parts of Denver</a>, to varying degrees, with <a href="/wiki/Plutonium-239" title="Plutonium-239">plutonium-239</a>, a harmful radioactive substance with a half-life of 24,200 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moore2007_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moore2007-37">[37]</a></sup> A study by the Jefferson County health director, Dr. Carl Johnson, in 1981 linked the contamination to an increase in birth defects and cancer incidence in central Denver and nearer Rocky Flats. Later studies confirmed many of his findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Plutonium contamination was still present outside the former plant site as of August 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENS-41">[41]</a></sup> and presents risks to building the envisioned Jefferson Parkway,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> which would complete Denver's automotive <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">beltway</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1146" data-file-width="1800" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg/220px-6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg/330px-6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg/440px-6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:6408-DenSkyline-BrownPalaceCosmoHotels.Jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downtown Denver cityscape, 1964. Includes Denver's oldest church (Trinity United Methodist), first building of the Mile High Center complex, Lincoln Center, old brownstone part of the Brown Palace Hotel, and Cosmopolitan Hotel – since demolished.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Denver was selected in 1970 to host the <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">1976 Winter Olympics</a> to coincide with Colorado's centennial celebration, but in November 1972 Colorado voters struck down ballot initiatives allocating public funds to pay for the high costs of the games, which were subsequently moved to <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck" title="Innsbruck">Innsbruck</a>, Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1970Olympics_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-1970Olympics-43">[43]</a></sup> The notoriety of becoming the only city ever to decline to host an Olympiad after being selected has made subsequent bids difficult. The movement against hosting the games was based largely on environmental issues and was led by State Representative <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lamm" title="Richard Lamm">Richard Lamm</a>, who was subsequently elected to three terms (1975–87) as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Colorado_Governors" title="List of Colorado Governors">Colorado governor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Denver explored a potential bid for the <a href="/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics" title="2022 Winter Olympics">2022 Winter Olympics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> but no bid will be submitted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In 2010, Denver adopted a comprehensive update of its zoning code.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The new zoning was developed to guide development as envisioned in adopted plans such as Blueprint Denver,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Transit Oriented Development Strategic Plan, Greenprint Denver, and the Strategic Transportation Plan.</p>
<p>Denver has also been known historically as the <i>Queen City of the Plains</i> and the <i>Queen City of the West</i>, because of its important role in the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_the_United_States" title="Agriculture in the United States">agricultural</a> industry of the high-plains region in eastern Colorado and along the foothills of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_Front_Range" title="Colorado Front Range">Colorado Front Range</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">US Navy</a> ships have been named <a href="/wiki/USS_Denver" title="USS Denver">USS <i>Denver</i></a> in honor of the city.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Denver" title="Geography of Denver">Geography of Denver</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1408px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:City_Park_Panorama_2_edited.png" title="Panorama of Denver in early May, as seen from the Denver Museum of Nature and Science. </div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2012" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg/220px-Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg/330px-Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg/440px-Denver_Colorado_from_space.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_from_Highlands.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1010" data-file-width="2186" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Denver_from_Highlands.jpg/220px-Denver_from_Highlands.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Denver_from_Highlands.jpg/330px-Denver_from_Highlands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Denver_from_Highlands.jpg/440px-Denver_from_Highlands.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

Downtown Denver in 2007, looking southeast from the Highland neighborhood.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SAM_0417.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2160" data-file-width="3840" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/SAM_0417.JPG/220px-SAM_0417.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/SAM_0417.JPG/330px-SAM_0417.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/SAM_0417.JPG/440px-SAM_0417.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SAM_0417.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sunrise in Denver on a typical January morning</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Denver is located in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>, between the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> to the west and the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a> to the east. Denver's topography consists of plains in the city center with hilly areas to the north, west and south. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> the city has a total area of 155 square miles (401 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 153 square miles (396 km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 1.6 square miles (4.1 km<sup>2</sup>) (1.1%) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-49">[49]</a></sup> The City and County of Denver is surrounded by only three other counties: <a href="/wiki/Adams_County,_Colorado" title="Adams County, Colorado">Adams County</a> to the north and east, <a href="/wiki/Arapahoe_County,_Colorado" title="Arapahoe County, Colorado">Arapahoe County</a> to the south and east, and <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Colorado" title="Jefferson County, Colorado">Jefferson County</a> to the west.</p>
<p>Although Denver's nickname is the "Mile-High City" because its official elevation is one mile above sea level, defined by the elevation of the spot of a benchmark on the steps of the State Capitol building, the elevation of the entire city ranges from 5,130 to 5,690 feet (1,560 to 1,730 m). According to <a href="/wiki/Geographic_Names_Information_System" title="Geographic Names Information System">Geographic Names Information System</a> (GNIS) and the <a href="/wiki/National_Elevation_Dataset" title="National Elevation Dataset">National Elevation Dataset</a>, the city's elevation is 5,278 feet (1,609 m), which is reflected on various websites such as that of the <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Denver_neighborhoods" title="List of Denver neighborhoods">List of Denver neighborhoods</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denveneighborhoods.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="541" data-file-width="729" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Denveneighborhoods.gif/400px-Denveneighborhoods.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Denveneighborhoods.gif/600px-Denveneighborhoods.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d7/Denveneighborhoods.gif 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denveneighborhoods.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Denver's 78 official neighborhoods</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1644" data-file-width="2918" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Denver.jpg/220px-Denver.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Denver.jpg/330px-Denver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Denver.jpg/440px-Denver.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Downtown_Denver" title="Downtown Denver">Downtown Denver</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of January 2013, the City and County of Denver has defined 78 official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighborhood" title="Neighborhood">neighborhoods</a> that the city and community groups use for planning and administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Although the city's delineation of the neighborhood boundaries is somewhat arbitrary, it corresponds roughly to the definitions used by residents. These "neighborhoods" should not be confused with cities or suburbs, which may be separate entities within the metro area.</p>
<p>The character of the neighborhoods varies significantly from one to another and includes everything from large skyscrapers to houses from the late 19th century to modern, suburban style developments. Generally, the neighborhoods closest to the city center are denser, older and contain more brick building material. Many neighborhoods away from the city center were developed after World War II, and are built with more modern materials and style. Some of the neighborhoods even farther from the city center, or recently redeveloped parcels anywhere in the city have either very suburban characteristics or are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_urbanism" title="New urbanism">new urbanist</a> developments that attempt to recreate the feel of older neighborhoods. Most neighborhoods contain parks or other features that are the focal point for the neighborhood.</p>
<p>Denver does not have larger area designations, <a href="/wiki/Community_areas_in_Chicago" title="Community areas in Chicago">unlike the City of Chicago</a>, which has larger areas that house the neighborhoods (IE: Northwest Side). Denver residents use the terms "north" "south" "east" and "west".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Construction_Cherokee.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Construction_Cherokee.jpg/220px-Construction_Cherokee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Construction_Cherokee.jpg/330px-Construction_Cherokee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Construction_Cherokee.jpg/440px-Construction_Cherokee.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Construction_Cherokee.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Construction along Cherokee Street in the Golden Triangle neighborhood.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Denver also has a number of neighborhoods not reflected in the administrative boundaries. These neighborhoods may reflect the way people in an area identify themselves or they might reflect how others, such as real estate developers, have defined those areas. Well-known non-administrative neighborhoods include the historic and trendy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LoDo" title="LoDo">LoDo</a> (short for "Lower Downtown"), part of the city's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station,_Denver" title="Union Station, Denver">Union Station neighborhood</a>; Uptown, straddling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Capitol_Hill,_Denver,_Colorado" title="North Capitol Hill, Denver, Colorado">North Capitol Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/City_Park_West,_Denver" title="City Park West, Denver">City Park West</a>; Curtis Park, part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Points_(Denver)" title="Five Points (Denver)">Five Points</a> neighborhood; <a href="/wiki/Alamo_Placita,_Denver" title="Alamo Placita, Denver">Alamo Placita</a>, the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Speer,_Denver" title="Speer, Denver">Speer neighborhood</a>; <a href="/wiki/Park_Hill,_Denver" title="Park Hill, Denver">Park Hill</a>, a successful example of intentional racial integration;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle,_Denver" title="Golden Triangle, Denver">Golden Triangle</a>, in the Civic Center.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_counties.2C_municipalities_and_CDPs">Adjacent counties, municipalities and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_designated_place" title="Census designated place">CDP</a>s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Adjacent counties, municipalities and CDPs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width:35%; text-align:center;"></td>
<td style="width:30%; text-align:center;"><b>North:</b> <i><b><a href="/wiki/Adams_County,_Colorado" title="Adams County, Colorado">Adams County</a></b></i>, <a href="/wiki/Berkley,_Colorado" title="Berkley, Colorado">Berkley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northglenn,_Colorado" title="Northglenn, Colorado">Northglenn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commerce_City,_Colorado" title="Commerce City, Colorado">Commerce City</a></td>
<td style="width:35%; text-align:center;"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width:10%; text-align:center;"><b>West:</b> <i><b><a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Colorado" title="Jefferson County, Colorado">Jefferson County</a></b></i>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat_Ridge,_Colorado" title="Wheat Ridge, Colorado">Wheat Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakeside,_Colorado" title="Lakeside, Colorado">Lakeside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_Colorado" title="Mountain View, Colorado">Mountain View</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgewater,_Colorado" title="Edgewater, Colorado">Edgewater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakewood,_Colorado" title="Lakewood, Colorado">Lakewood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dakota_Ridge,_Colorado" title="Dakota Ridge, Colorado">Dakota Ridge</a></td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="966" data-file-width="2779" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG/350px-Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG/525px-Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG/700px-Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Skyline_in_Winter.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of downtown Denver after a snowstorm in March 2016, looking northwest from <a href="/wiki/Cheesman_Park,_Denver" title="Cheesman Park, Denver">Cheesman Park</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Denver lies within the <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continentality" title="Continentality">continental</a> climate zone (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" title="Cold semi-arid climate">BSk</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> It has four distinct seasons and receives a modest amount of precipitation spread throughout the year. Due to its inland location on the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a>, at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>, Denver, like all cities along the eastern edge of the Rocky Mountains, is subject to sudden changes in weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Contrary to the popular belief that Denver receives 300 days of sunshine a year, the city can actually expect to receive an average of 115 clear days, 130 partly cloudy days, and 120 cloudy days each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>July is the warmest month, with a daily average temperature of 74.2 °F (23.4 °C). Summers range from mild to hot with occasional, sometimes severe, afternoon thunderstorms and high temperatures reaching 90 °F (32 °C) on 38 days annually, and occasionally 100 °F (38 °C). December, the coldest month of the year, has a daily average temperature of 29.9 °F (−1.2 °C). Winters consist of periods of snow and very low temperatures alternating with periods of milder weather due to the warming effect of <a href="/wiki/Chinook_wind" title="Chinook wind">Chinook winds</a>. In winter, daytime highs can exceed 60 °F (16 °C) but can also often fail to reach 32 °F (0 °C) during periods of cold weather and can even fail to rise above 0 °F (−18 °C) on occasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> On the coldest nights of the year, lows can easily fall to −10 °F (−23 °C) or below. Snowfall is common throughout the late fall, winter and early spring, averaging 53.5 inches (136 cm) for 1981–2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-60">[60]</a></sup> The average window for measurable (≥0.1 in or 0.25 cm) snow is October 17 through April 27; although, measurable snowfall has fallen in Denver as early as September 4 and as late as June 3. Extremes in temperature range from −29 °F (−34 °C) on January 9, 1875 up to 105 °F (41 °C) as recently as <a href="/wiki/Summer_2012_North_American_heat_wave" title="Summer 2012 North American heat wave">June 25 and 26, 2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Due to the city's high elevation and aridity, <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal temperature variation</a> is large throughout the year.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">Tornadoes</a> are rare west of the I-25 corridor; however, one notable exception was an <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">F3</a> tornado that struck 4.4 miles south of downtown on June 15, 1988. On the other hand, the suburbs east of Denver and the city's east-northeastern extension (<a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a>) can see a few tornadoes, often weak <a href="/wiki/Landspout" title="Landspout">landspout</a> tornadoes, each spring and summer—especially during June with the enhancement of the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Convergence_Vorticity_Zone" title="Denver Convergence Vorticity Zone">Denver Convergence Vorticity Zone</a> (DCVZ). The DCVZ, also known as the Denver Cyclone, is a variable vortex of storm-forming air flow usually found north and east of downtown, and which often includes the airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Heavy weather from the DCVZ can disrupt airport operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In a study looking at <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a> events in areas with a population of at least 50,000, Denver was found to be ranked 10th most prone to hail storms in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">continental United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In fact, Denver has received two of the top 10 <a href="/wiki/List_of_costly_or_deadly_hailstorms" title="List of costly or deadly hailstorms">costliest hailstorms</a> in United States history which occurred on July 11, 1990 and July 20, 2009, respectively.</p>
<p>Based on 30-year averages obtained from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Climatic_Data_Center" title="National Climatic Data Center">National Climatic Data Center</a> for the months of December, January and February, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weather_Channel" title="Weather Channel">Weather Channel</a> ranked Denver the 18th coldest major U.S. city as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><br/></p>

<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>, the population of the City and County of Denver was 600,158, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">24th most populous U.S. city</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCounty_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCounty-77">[75]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Lakewood,_CO_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora-Lakewood, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Lakewood, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> had an estimated 2013 population of 2,697,476 and ranked as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">21st most populous U.S. metropolitan statistical area</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-15">[15]</a></sup> and the larger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Boulder_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora-Boulder Combined Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Boulder Combined Statistical Area</a> had an estimated 2013 population of 3,277,309 and ranked as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Combined_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Combined Statistical Areas">16th most populous U.S. metropolitan area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-15">[15]</a></sup> Denver is the most populous city within a <a href="/wiki/Radius" title="Radius">radius</a> centered in the city and of 550 miles (885 km) magnitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-15">[15]</a></sup> Denverites is a term used for residents of Denver.</p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>, the City and County of Denver contains 600,158 people and 285,797 households. The population density is 3,698 inhabitants per square mile (1,428/km²) including the airport. There are 285,797 housing units at an average density of 1,751 per square mile (676/km²).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-QF-14">[14]</a></sup> However, the average density throughout most Denver neighborhoods tends to be higher. Without the 80249 zip code (47.3 sq mi, 8,407 residents) near the airport, the average density increases to around 5,470 per square mile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-City-Data.com_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-City-Data.com-78">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, the racial composition of Denver was as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a>: 68.9% (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">Non-Hispanic Whites</a>: 52.2%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> (of any race): 31.8%; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">Mexican Americans</a> made up 24.9% of the city's population.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black or African American</a>: 10.2%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>: 3.4% (0.8% Vietnamese, 0.6% Chinese, 0.5% Indian, 0.3% Korean, 0.3% Japanese, 0.3% Filipino, 0.2% Burmese, 0.1% Cambodian)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a>: 1.4%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">Native Hawaiian and Other Pacific Islander</a>: 0.1%</li>
<li>Some other race: 9.2%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a>: 4.1%</li>
</ul>
<p>Approximately 70.3% of the population (over five years old) spoke only English at home. An additional 23.5% of the population spoke Spanish at home. In terms of ancestry, 31.2% were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American" title="Mexican-American">Mexican</a>, 14.6% of the population were of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a> ancestry, 9.7% were of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> ancestry, 8.9% were of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> ancestry, and 4.0% were of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> ancestry.</p>
<p>There are 250,906 households, of which 23.2% have children under the age of 18 living with them, 34.7% are married couples living together, 10.8% have a female householder with no husband present, and 50.1% are non-families. 39.3% of all households are made up of individuals and 9.4% have someone living alone who is 65 years of age or older. The average household size is 2.27 and the average family size is 3.14.</p>
<p>Age distribution is 22.0% under the age of 18, 10.7% from 18 to 24, 36.1% from 25 to 44, 20.0% from 45 to 64, and 11.3% who are 65 years of age or older. The median age is 33 years. For every 100 females there are 102.1 males.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_household_income" title="Median household income">median household income</a> is $45,438, and the median family income is $48,195. Males have a median income of $36,232 versus $33,768 for females. The per capita income for the city is $24,101. 19.1% of the population and 14.6% of families are below the poverty line. Out of the total population, 25.3% of those under the age of 18 and 13.7% of those 65 and older are living below the poverty line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 72.28% (386,815) of Denver residents aged five and older spoke only <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at home, while 21.42% (114,635) spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 0.85% (4,550) <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, 0.57% (3,073) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">African languages</a>, 0.53% (2,845) <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, 0.50% (2,681) <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, 0.47% (2,527) <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, and 0.46% (2,465) <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>. In total, 27.72% (148,335) of Denver's population age five and older spoke a language other than English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup></p>

The 17th street district includes many financial, business and corporate buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Mint_in_Denver,_CO_IMG_5527.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/U.S._Mint_in_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5527.JPG/220px-U.S._Mint_in_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5527.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/U.S._Mint_in_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5527.JPG/330px-U.S._Mint_in_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5527.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/U.S._Mint_in_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5527.JPG/440px-U.S._Mint_in_Denver%2C_CO_IMG_5527.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Mint_in_Denver,_CO_IMG_5527.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Mint" title="United States Mint">United States Mint</a> in Denver (2010)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Denver MSA has a gross metropolitan product of $157.6 billion in 2010, making it the 18th largest metro economy in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> Denver's economy is based partially on its geographic position and its connection to some of the major transportation systems of the country. Because Denver is the largest city within 500 miles (800 km), it has become a natural location for storage and distribution of goods and services to the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">Mountain States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwest states</a>, as well as all <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">western states</a>. Another benefit for distribution is that Denver is nearly equidistant from large cities of the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a>, such as Chicago and <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a> and some large cities of the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a>, such as Los Angeles and San Francisco.</p>
<p>Over the years, the city has been home to other large corporations in the central United States, making Denver a key trade point for the country. Several well-known companies originated in or have relocated to Denver. William Ainsworth opened the Denver Instrument Company in 1895 to make analytical balances for gold assayers. Its factory is now in <a href="/wiki/Arvada,_Colorado" title="Arvada, Colorado">Arvada</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIMCO" title="AIMCO">AIMCO</a> (NYSE: AIV)—the largest owner and operator of apartment communities in the United States, with approximately 870 communities comprising nearly 136,000 units in 44 states—is headquartered in Denver, employing approximately 3,500 people. Also <a href="/wiki/Samsonite" title="Samsonite">Samsonite</a> Corp., the world's largest luggage manufacturer, began in Denver in 1910 as Shwayder Trunk Manufacturing Company, but Samsonite closed its NE Denver factory in 2001, and moved its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> after a change of ownership in 2006. The <a href="/wiki/Qwest_Corporation" title="Qwest Corporation">Mountain States Telephone &amp; Telegraph Company</a>, founded in Denver in 1911, is now a part of telecommunications giant <a href="/wiki/CenturyLink" title="CenturyLink">CenturyLink</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/MediaNews_Group" title="MediaNews Group">MediaNews Group</a> purchased the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_Post" title="Denver Post">Denver Post</a></i> in 1987; the company is based in Denver. The <a href="/wiki/Gates_Corporation" title="Gates Corporation">Gates Corporation</a>, the world's largest producer of automotive belts and hoses, was established in S. Denver in 1919. <a href="/wiki/Russell_Stover_Candies" title="Russell Stover Candies">Russell Stover Candies</a> Inc. made its first chocolate candy in Denver in 1923, but moved to Kansas City in 1969. The Wright &amp; McGill Company has been making its Eagle Claw brand of fishing gear in NE Denver since 1925. The original <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines_(1950%E2%80%931986)" title="Frontier Airlines (1950–1986)">Frontier Airlines</a> began operations at Denver's old <a href="/wiki/Stapleton_International_Airport" title="Stapleton International Airport">Stapleton International Airport</a> in 1950. <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier</a> was reincarnated at <a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">DIA</a> in 1994. Scott's Liquid Gold, Inc., has been making furniture polish in Denver since 1954. <a href="/wiki/Village_Inn" title="Village Inn">Village Inn</a> restaurants began as a single pancake house in Denver in 1958. <a href="/wiki/Big_O_Tires" title="Big O Tires">Big O Tires</a>, LLC, of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centennial,_CO" title="Centennial, CO">Centennial</a> opened its first franchise in 1962 in Denver. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Shane_Company" title="The Shane Company">The Shane Company</a> sold its first diamond jewelry in 1971 in Denver. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johns-Manville" title="Johns-Manville">Johns Manville</a> Corp., a manufacturer of insulation and roofing products, relocated its headquarters to Denver from New York in 1972. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CH2M_HILL" title="CH2M HILL">CH2M HILL</a> Inc., an engineering and construction firm, relocated from Oregon to the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Technological_Center" title="Denver Technological Center">Denver Technological Center</a> in 1980. The <a href="/wiki/Ball_Corporation" title="Ball Corporation">Ball Corporation</a> sold its glass business in Indiana in the 1990s and moved to suburban <a href="/wiki/Broomfield,_Colorado" title="Broomfield, Colorado">Broomfield</a>. Ball has several operations in greater Denver.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Molson_Coors_Brewing_Company" title="Molson Coors Brewing Company">Molson Coors Brewing Company</a> established its U.S. headquarters in Denver in 2005. Its subsidiary and regional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wholesale" title="Wholesale">wholesale</a> distributor, Coors Distributing Company, is in NW Denver. The <a href="/wiki/Newmont_Mining_Corporation" title="Newmont Mining Corporation">Newmont Mining Corporation</a>, the 2nd largest gold producer in North America and one of the largest in the world, is headquartered in Denver.</p>
<p>Large Denver-area employers that have headquarters elsewhere include <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a> Corp., <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kroger" title="Kroger">Kroger</a> Co. and <a href="/wiki/Xcel_Energy" title="Xcel Energy">Xcel Energy</a>, Inc. <a class="external text" href="http://company.mapquest.com/" rel="nofollow">MapQuest</a>, an online site for maps, directions and business listings, is headquartered in Denver's LoDo district.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Union_Station_Development.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Union_Station_Development.jpg/220px-Union_Station_Development.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Union_Station_Development.jpg/330px-Union_Station_Development.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Union_Station_Development.jpg/440px-Union_Station_Development.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Union_Station_Development.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Development in the bustling Union Station section of downtown.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Geography also allows Denver to have a considerable government presence, with many federal agencies based or having offices in the Denver area. Along with federal agencies come many companies based on US defense and space projects, and more jobs are brought to the city by virtue of its being the capital of the state of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>. The Denver area is home to the former nuclear weapons plant <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Flats_Plant" title="Rocky Flats Plant">Rocky Flats</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Federal_Center" title="Denver Federal Center">Denver Federal Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byron_G._Rogers_Federal_Building_and_United_States_Courthouse" title="Byron G. Rogers Federal Building and United States Courthouse">Byron G. Rogers Federal Building and United States Courthouse</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Mint" title="Denver Mint">Denver Mint</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Laboratory" title="National Renewable Energy Laboratory">National Renewable Energy Laboratory</a>.</p>
<p>In 2005, a $310.7 million expansion for the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Convention_Center" title="Colorado Convention Center">Colorado Convention Center</a> was completed, doubling its size. The hope was that the center's expansion would elevate the city to one of the top 10 cities in the nation for holding a convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Denver's position near the mineral-rich <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> encouraged mining and energy companies to spring up in the area. In the early days of the city, gold and silver booms and busts played a large role in the economic success of the city. In the 1970s and early 1980s, the energy crisis in America and resulting high oil prices created an energy boom in Denver captured in the soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/Dynasty_(TV_series)" title="Dynasty (TV series)">Dynasty</a></i>. Denver was built up considerably during this time with the construction of many new downtown skyscrapers. When the price of oil dropped from $34 a barrel in 1981 to $9 a barrel in 1986, the Denver economy dropped with it, leaving almost 15,000 oil industry workers in the area unemployed (including former mayor and current governor <a href="/wiki/John_Hickenlooper" title="John Hickenlooper">John Hickenlooper</a>, a former geologist), and the highest office vacancy rate in the nation (30%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> Since then, the industry has recovered and there remain 700 employed petroleum engineers in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> Advances in hydraulic fracturing have made the DJ Basin of Colorado into an accessible and lucrative oil play. Energy and mining are still important in Denver's economy today, with companies such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EnCana" title="EnCana">EnCana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halliburton" title="Halliburton">Halliburton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smith_International" title="Smith International">Smith International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto Group</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newmont_Mining" title="Newmont Mining">Newmont Mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noble_Energy" title="Noble Energy">Noble Energy</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anadarko_Petroleum_Corporation" title="Anadarko Petroleum Corporation">Anadarko</a> headquartered or having significant operations in the area.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg/220px-University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg/330px-University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg/440px-University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first Chipotle Mexican Grill near the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Denver's west-central geographic location in the Mountain Time Zone (UTC−7) also benefits the telecommunications industry by allowing communication with both North American coasts, South America, Europe, and Asia in the same business day. Denver's location on the 105th meridian at over one mile (1.6 km) in elevation also enables it to be the largest city in the U.S. to offer a "one-bounce" real-time satellite uplink to six continents in the same business day. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qwest_Communications" title="Qwest Communications">Qwest Communications</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dish_Network_Corporation" title="Dish Network Corporation">Dish Network Corporation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starz_(TV_network)" title="Starz (TV network)">Starz-Encore</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DIRECTV" title="DIRECTV">DIRECTV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a> are a few of the many telecommunications companies with operations in the Denver area. These and other high-tech companies had a boom in Denver in the mid to late 1990s. Denver had one of the lowest unemployment rates in the nation at 3.8% in October 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> As of April 2015, the unemployment rate for the Denver-Aurora-Broomfield MSA is 4.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> The Downtown region has seen increased real estate investment with the construction of several new skyscrapers from 2010 onward and major development around <a href="/wiki/Denver_Union_Station" title="Denver Union Station">Denver Union Station</a>.</p>
<p>Denver has also enjoyed success as a pioneer in the fast casual restaurant industry, with many popular national chain restaurants founded and based in Denver. <a href="/wiki/Chipotle_Mexican_Grill" title="Chipotle Mexican Grill">Chipotle Mexican Grill</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quizno%27s" title="Quizno's">Quizno's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Smashburger" title="Smashburger">Smashburger</a> were founded and headquartered in Denver. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qdoba_Mexican_Grill" title="Qdoba Mexican Grill">Qdoba Mexican Grill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noodles_%26_Company" title="Noodles &amp; Company">Noodles &amp; Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Good_Times_Burgers_%26_Frozen_Custard" title="Good Times Burgers &amp; Frozen Custard">Good Times Burgers &amp; Frozen Custard</a> originated in Denver, but have moved their headquarters to the nearby suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Wheat_Ridge,_Colorado" title="Wheat Ridge, Colorado">Wheat Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broomfield,_Colorado" title="Broomfield, Colorado">Broomfield</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Golden,_Colorado" title="Golden, Colorado">Golden</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>In 2015, Denver ranked No. 1 on <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>'</i> list of the Best Places for Business and Careers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_contemporary_life">Culture and contemporary life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture and contemporary life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landmarks_of_Denver" title="Landmarks of Denver">Landmarks of Denver</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_in_Denver" title="Music in Denver">Music in Denver</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG/220px-Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG/330px-Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG/440px-Coloradoconventioncenter01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Colorado_Convention_Center" title="Colorado Convention Center">Colorado Convention Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DenverPavillion.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/DenverPavillion.JPG/220px-DenverPavillion.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/DenverPavillion.JPG/330px-DenverPavillion.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/DenverPavillion.JPG/440px-DenverPavillion.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

Denver Pavilions is a popular arts, entertainment, and shopping center on the <a href="/wiki/16th_Street_Mall" title="16th Street Mall">16th Street Mall</a> in downtown Denver.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg/220px-Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg/330px-Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg/440px-Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex" title="Denver Performing Arts Complex">Denver Performing Arts Complex</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Apollo Hall opened quickly after the city's founding in 1859 and staged many plays for eager settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenverHist_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-DenverHist-23">[23]</a></sup> In the 1880s <a href="/wiki/Horace_Tabor" title="Horace Tabor">Horace Tabor</a> built Denver's first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opera_House" title="Opera House">Opera House</a>. After the start of the 20th century, city leaders embarked on a city beautification program that created many of the city's parks, parkways, museums, and the Municipal Auditorium, which was home to the <a href="/wiki/1908_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1908 Democratic National Convention">1908 Democratic National Convention</a> and is now known as the <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Caulkins_Opera_House" title="Ellie Caulkins Opera House">Ellie Caulkins Opera House</a>. Denver and the metropolitan areas around it continued to support culture. In 1988, voters in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_Metropolitan_Area" title="Denver Metropolitan Area">Denver Metropolitan Area</a> approved the Scientific and Cultural Facilities Tax (commonly known as SCFD), a 1 cent <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> that contributes money to various cultural and scientific facilities and organizations throughout the Metro area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> The tax was renewed by voters in 1994 and 2004 and allows the SCFD to operate until 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Denver is home to many nationally recognized museums, including a new wing for the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Art_Museum" title="Denver Art Museum">Denver Art Museum</a> by world-renowned architect <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Libeskind" title="Daniel Libeskind">Daniel Libeskind</a>, the second largest <a href="/wiki/Denver_Performing_Arts_Complex" title="Denver Performing Arts Complex">Performing Arts Center</a> in the nation after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lincoln_Center" title="Lincoln Center">Lincoln Center</a> in New York City and bustling neighborhoods such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LoDo" title="LoDo">LoDo</a>, filled with art galleries, restaurants, bars and clubs. That is part of the reason why Denver was recently recognized for the third year in a row as the best city for singles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> Denver's neighborhoods also continue their influx of diverse people and businesses while the city's cultural institutions grow and prosper. The city acquired the estate of <a href="/wiki/Abstract_expressionism" title="Abstract expressionism">abstract expressionist</a> painter <a href="/wiki/Clyfford_Still" title="Clyfford Still">Clyfford Still</a> in 2004 and built a museum to exhibit his works near the Denver Art Museum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science" title="Denver Museum of Nature and Science">Denver Museum of Nature and Science</a> currently holds an aquamarine specimen valued at over one million dollars, as well as specimens of the state mineral, rhodochrosite. Every September the Denver Mart, located at 451 E. 58th Avenue hosts a gem and mineral show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minaral_show_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-minaral_show-93">[91]</a></sup> The state history museum, <a href="/wiki/History_Colorado_Center" title="History Colorado Center">History Colorado Center</a>, opened in April 2012. It features hands-on and interactive exhibits, artifacts and programs about Colorado history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> It was named in 2013 by <i><a href="/wiki/True_West_Magazine" title="True West Magazine">True West Magazine</a></i> as one of the top-ten "must see" history museums in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> History Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Byers-Evans_House" title="Byers-Evans House">Byers-Evans House</a> Museum and the <a href="/wiki/Molly_Brown_House" title="Molly Brown House">Molly Brown House</a> are nearby.</p>
<p>Denver has numerous art districts around the city, including Denver's Art District on Santa Fe and the River North Art District (RiNo).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sante_Fe_Arts_District_(Denver,_Colorado_-_17_December_2003).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="2032" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Sante_Fe_Arts_District_%28Denver%2C_Colorado_-_17_December_2003%29.jpg/220px-Sante_Fe_Arts_District_%28Denver%2C_Colorado_-_17_December_2003%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Sante_Fe_Arts_District_%28Denver%2C_Colorado_-_17_December_2003%29.jpg/330px-Sante_Fe_Arts_District_%28Denver%2C_Colorado_-_17_December_2003%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Sante_Fe_Arts_District_%28Denver%2C_Colorado_-_17_December_2003%29.jpg/440px-Sante_Fe_Arts_District_%28Denver%2C_Colorado_-_17_December_2003%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
