<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colfaxatauraria.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Denver RTD Light Rail car at the "Colfax at Auraria" station</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station,_December_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2295" data-file-width="3440" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station%2C_December_2014.jpg/220px-Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station%2C_December_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station%2C_December_2014.jpg/330px-Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station%2C_December_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station%2C_December_2014.jpg/440px-Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station%2C_December_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Main_Facade_of_Denver_Union_Station,_December_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Denver,_Colorado)" title="Union Station (Denver, Colorado)">Denver Union Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">Mass transportation</a> throughout the <a href="/wiki/Denver_metropolitan_area" title="Denver metropolitan area">Denver metropolitan area</a> is managed and coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Transportation_District" title="Regional Transportation District">Regional Transportation District</a> (RTD). RTD currently operates more than 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a> serving over 10,000 bus stops in 38 municipal jurisdictions in eight counties around the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Boulder_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Denver-Aurora-Boulder Combined Statistical Area">Denver and Boulder metropolitan areas</a>. Additionally, RTD operates seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TheRide" title="TheRide">rail</a> lines, the A, C, D, E, F, W, and H with a total of 57.9 miles (93.2 km) of track, serving 44 stations. All lines are light rail except the A, a commuter rail line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/FasTracks" title="FasTracks">FasTracks</a> is a light rail/bus/rail expansion project approved by voters in 2004 which will serve neighboring suburbs and communities. The W line, or West line, opened in April 2013 serving Golden/Federal Center.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Colorado_Department_of_Transportation" title="Colorado Department of Transportation">CDOT</a> runs a bus system named Bustang that offers weekday service between Union Station in Denver, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glenwood_Springs" title="Glenwood Springs">Glenwood Springs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs" title="Colorado Springs">Colorado Springs</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Collins" title="Fort Collins">Fort Collins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Union_Station,_Opening_Day.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Union_Station%2C_Opening_Day.jpg/220px-Union_Station%2C_Opening_Day.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Union_Station%2C_Opening_Day.jpg/330px-Union_Station%2C_Opening_Day.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Union_Station%2C_Opening_Day.jpg/440px-Union_Station%2C_Opening_Day.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Union_Station,_Opening_Day.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Union Station train shed, designed by Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill, on opening day of the A line to DIA.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound Lines</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercity_bus" title="Intercity bus">intercity bus</a> operator, has a major hub in Denver, with routes to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reno,_Nevada" title="Reno, Nevada">Reno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, and their headquarters, <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>. Subsidiary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autobuses_Americanos" title="Autobuses Americanos">Autobuses Americanos</a> provides service to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Paso" title="El Paso">El Paso</a>. Allied bus operators Black Hills Trailways, and <a href="/wiki/Burlington_Trailways" title="Burlington Trailways">Burlington Trailways</a> provide service to <a href="/wiki/Billings,_Montana" title="Billings, Montana">Billings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alamosa,_Colorado" title="Alamosa, Colorado">Alamosa</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, the national passenger rail system, provides service to Denver, operating its <i><a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyr</a></i> daily in both directions between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Chicago)" title="Union Station (Chicago)">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emeryville,_California" title="Emeryville, California">Emeryville</a>, California, across the bay from San Francisco. Amtrak Thruway service operated by private bus companies links the Denver station with Rocky Mountain points.</p>
<p>At Albuquerque, New Mexico, Denver Thruway connections are made daily with the Amtrak <i><a href="/wiki/Southwest_Chief" title="Southwest Chief">Southwest Chief</a></i>. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Ski_Train" title="Ski Train">Ski Train</a> operated on the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver_%26_Rio_Grande_Western_Railroad" title="Denver &amp; Rio Grande Western Railroad">Denver &amp; Rio Grande Western Railroad</a>, which took passengers between Denver and the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Park,_Colorado" title="Winter Park, Colorado">Winter Park</a> Ski Resort, but it is no longer in service. The Ski Train made its final run to Winter Park on March 29, 2009.</p>
<p>Denver's early years as a major train hub of the west are still very visible today. Trains stop in Denver at historic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Denver)" title="Union Station (Denver)">Union Station</a>, where travelers can access RTD's 16th Street Free MallRide or use light rail to tour the city. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Denver)" title="Union Station (Denver)">Union Station</a> will also serve as the main juncture for rail travel in the metro area, at the completion of <a href="/wiki/FasTracks" title="FasTracks">FasTracks</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg/220px-Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg/330px-Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg/440px-Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport_terminal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Inside the main terminal of <a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/220px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/330px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/440px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Outside view of the main terminal, DIA</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a> (IATA: DEN, ICAO: KDEN), commonly known as DIA, serves as the primary airport for a large region surrounding Denver. DIA is located 18.6 miles (30 km) east-northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_Capitol" title="Colorado State Capitol">Colorado State Capitol</a>. DIA is the tenth busiest airport in the world and ranks fourth in the United States, with 51,245,334 passengers passing through it in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> It covers more than 53 square miles (137.3 km<sup>2</sup>), making it the largest airport by land area in the United States and larger than the island of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> Denver serves as a major hub for <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, is the headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier Airlines</a>, and is the fastest-growing <a href="/wiki/Focus_city" title="Focus city">focus city</a> for <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a>.</p>
<p>Three <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> airports serve the Denver area. <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Rocky Mountain Metropolitan Airport">Rocky Mountain Metropolitan Airport</a> (KBJC) is 13.7 miles (22 km) north-northwest, <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Airport" title="Centennial Airport">Centennial Airport</a> (KAPA) is 13.7 miles (22 km) south-southeast, and <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Airport" title="Front Range Airport">Front Range Airport</a> (KFTG) is located 23.7 miles (38 km) east of the state capitol.</p>
<p>In the past, Denver has been home to several other airports that are no longer operational. <a href="/wiki/Stapleton_International_Airport" title="Stapleton International Airport">Stapleton International Airport</a> was closed in 1995 when it was replaced by DIA. <a href="/wiki/Lowry_Air_Force_Base" title="Lowry Air Force Base">Lowry Air Force Base</a> was a military flight training facility that ceased flight operations in 1966, with the base finally being closed in 1994. It is currently being used for residential purposes. <a href="/wiki/Buckley_Air_Force_Base" title="Buckley Air Force Base">Buckley Air Force Base</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Air_National_Guard" title="Air National Guard">Air National Guard</a> base, is currently the only military facility in the Denver-Metro area.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_cities_of_Denver" title="Sister cities of Denver">Sister cities of Denver</a></div>
<p>Denver's relationship with <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest, France</a>, began in 1948, making it the second-oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">sister city</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> Since then, Denver has established relationships with additional sister cities, and currently has a total of ten partnerships:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a>, France, (1948)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Takayama,_Gifu" title="Takayama, Gifu">Takayama</a>, Japan (1960)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, Kenya (1975)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karmiel" title="Karmiel">Karmiel</a>, Israel (1977)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a>, Mexico (1983)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Potenza" title="Potenza">Potenza</a>, Italy (1983)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, India (1984)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kunming" title="Kunming">Kunming</a>, China (1985)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Axum" title="Axum">Axum</a>, Ethiopia (1995)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ulaanbaatar" title="Ulaanbaatar">Ulaanbaatar</a>, Mongolia (2001)</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition to these, the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Regional_Council_of_Governments" title="Denver Regional Council of Governments">Denver Regional Council of Governments</a> (consisting of the city and 51 other local governments) has established a "sister city" relationship with the <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Governorate" title="Baghdad Governorate">Baghdad Governorate</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>'s eighteen provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
